With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\\n704: // retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\\n705: //\\n706: // To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\\n707: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\\n708: \\tif cb == nil {\\n709: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n710: \\t}\\n711: \\n712: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n713: \\t\\treturn err\\n714: \\t}\\n715: \\n716: \\tm.lock.RLock()\\n717: \\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\\n718: \\n719: \\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\\n720: \\tmk := m.key.New()\\n721: \\tmv := m.value.New()\\n722: \\n723: \\ti := m.m.Iterate()\\n724: \\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\\n725: \\t\\tcb(mk, mv)\\n726: \\n727: \\t\\tmk = m.key.New()\\n728: \\t\\tmv = m.value.New()\\n729: \\t}\\n730: \\n731: \\treturn i.Err()\\n732: }\\n733: \\n734: // DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\\n735: // the slice of all values from all CPUs.\\n736: type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\\n737: \\n738: // DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\\n739: // DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\\n740: // from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\\n741: // to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\\n742: func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\\n743: \\tif cb == nil {\\n744: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n745: \\t}\\n746: \\n747: \\tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\\n748: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\\\", m.name)\\n749: \\t}\\n750: \\n751: \\tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\\n752: \\tif !ok {\\n753: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\\\", m.name)\\n754: \\t}\\n755: \\n756: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n757: \\t\\treturn err\\n758: \\t}\\n759: \\n760: \\tm.lock.RLock()\\n761: \\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\\n762: \\n763: \\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\\n764: \\tmk := m.key.New()\\n765: \\tmv := v.NewSlice()\\n766: \\n767: \\ti := m.m.Iterate()\\n768: \\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\\n769: \\t\\tcb(mk, mv)\\n770: \\n771: \\t\\tmk = m.key.New()\\n772: \\t\\tmv = v.NewSlice()\\n773: \\t}\\n774: \\n775: \\treturn i.Err()\\n776: }\\n777: \\n778: // DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\\n779: // if the given map does not exist.\\n780: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\\n781: \\tfound, err := m.exist()\\n782: \\tif err != nil {\\n783: \\t\\treturn err\\n784: \\t}\\n785: \\n786: \\tif found {\\n787: \\t\\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\\n788: \\t}\\n789: \\n790: \\treturn nil\\n791: }\\n792: \\n793: // DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\\n794: // additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\\n795: // element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\\n796: // can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\\n797: // In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\\n798: // the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\\n799: //\\n800: // The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\\n801: // object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\\n802: // not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\\n803: func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\\n804: \\tif cb == nil {\\n805: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n806: \\t}\\n807: \\n808: \\tif stats == nil {\\n809: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"stats is nil\\\")\\n810: \\t}\\n811: \\n812: \\tvar (\\n813: \\t\\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\\n814: \\t\\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\\n815: \\t\\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\\n816: \\t\\tvalue      = m.value.New()\\n817: \\n818: \\t\\tprevKeyValid = false\\n819: \\t)\\n820: \\n821: \\tstats.start()\\n822: \\tdefer stats.finish()\\n823: \\n824: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n825: \\t\\treturn err\\n826: \\t}\\n827: \\n828: \\t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\\n829: \\t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\\n830: \\t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\\n831: \\tm.lock.Lock()\\n832: \\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\\n833: \\tif m.m == nil {\\n834: \\t\\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\\n835: \\t\\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\\n836: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"map is closed\\\")\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\n839: \\t// Get the first map key.\\n840: \\tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\\n841: \\t\\tstats.Lookup = 1\\n842: \\t\\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\\n843: \\t\\t\\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\\n844: \\t\\t\\tstats.Completed = true\\n845: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n846: \\t\\t}\\n847: \\t}\\n848: \\n849: \\t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\\n850: \\t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\\n851: \\t// updated while being iterated)\\n852: \\tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\\n853: \\n854: \\t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\\n855: \\t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\\n856: \\t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\\n857: \\tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\\n858: \\t\\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\\n859: \\t\\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\\n860: \\t\\t//\\n861: \\t\\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\\n862: \\t\\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\\n863: \\t\\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\\n864: \\t\\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\\n865: \\t\\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\\n866: \\n867: \\t\\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\\n868: \\t\\t\\tstats.LookupFailed++\\n869: \\t\\t\\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\\n870: \\t\\t\\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\\n871: \\t\\t\\tif prevKeyValid {\\n872: \\t\\t\\t\\tcurrentKey = prevKey\\n873: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\\n874: \\t\\t\\t\\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\\n875: \\t\\t\\t\\tprevKeyValid = false\\n876: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.KeyFallback++\\n877: \\t\\t\\t} else {\\n878: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\\n879: \\t\\t\\t\\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\\n880: \\t\\t\\t\\t// one, or the first element in the map.\\n881: \\t\\t\\t\\tcurrentKey = nextKey\\n882: \\t\\t\\t\\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\\n883: \\t\\t\\t\\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\\n884: \\t\\t\\t\\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\\n885: \\t\\t\\t\\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\tnextKey = m.key.New()\\n887: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.Interrupted++\\n888: \\t\\t\\t}\\n889: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n890: \\t\\t}\\n891: \\n892: \\t\\tcb(currentKey, value)\\n893: \\n894: \\t\\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\\n895: \\t\\t\\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\\n896: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.Completed = true\\n897: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\\n898: \\t\\t\\t}\\n899: \\t\\t\\treturn nextKeyErr\\n900: \\t\\t}\\n901: \\n902: \\t\\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\\n903: \\t\\tprevKey = currentKey\\n904: \\t\\tcurrentKey = nextKey\\n905: \\t\\tnextKey = m.key.New()\\n906: \\t\\tprevKeyValid = true\\n907: \\t}\\n908: \\n909: \\treturn ErrMaxLookup\\n910: }\\n911: \\n912: // BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\\n913: // of bpf maps.\\n914: type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\\n915: \\tm    *Map\\n916: \\terr  error\\n917: \\tkeys \\treturn kvs.err\\n979: }\\n980: \\n981: func (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\\n982: \\tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\\n983: \\t\\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\\n984: \\t}\\n985: \\treturn defaultBatchedRetries\\n986: }\\n987: \\n988: const defaultBatchedRetries = 3\\n989: \\n990: type BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] retries\\n1013: \\t\\treturn in\\n1014: \\t}\\n1015: }\\n1016: \\n1017: // WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\\n1018: // chosen starting chunk size.\\n1019: func WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1020: \\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1021: \\t\\tin.chunkSize = size\\n1022: \\t\\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\\n1023: \\t\\t\\tin.chunkSize = 8\\n1024: \\t\\t}\\n1025: \\t\\treturn in\\n1026: \\t}\\n1027: }\\n1028: \\n1029: // CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\\n1030: // iterator.\\n1031: func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\\n1032: \\tc := 0\\n1033: \\tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\\n1034: \\t\\tc++\\n1035: \\t}\\n1036: \\treturn c, iter.Err()\\n1037: }\\n1038: \\n1039: func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\\n1040: \\tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\\n1041: \\tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\\n1042: \\treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\\n1043: }\\n1044: \\n1045: // IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\\n1046: // using the batched API.\\n1047: // In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\\n1048: // this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\\n1049: // of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\\n1050: // If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\\n1051: // will be returned via \\tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\\n1059: \\t\\tbreak\\n1060: \\tdefault:\\n1061: \\t\\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\\\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\\\", bi.m.Type())\\n1062: \\t\\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\\n1063: \\t}\\n1064: \\n1065: \\tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\\n1066: \\n1067: \\tfor _, opt := range opts {\\n1068: \\t\\tif opt != nil {\\n1069: \\t\\t\\tbi = opt(bi)\\n1070: \\t\\t}\\n1071: \\t}\\n1072: \\n1073: \\t// reset values\\n1074: \\tbi.err = nil\\n1075: \\tbi.batchSize = 0\\n1076: VP) bool) {\\n1082: \\t\\tif bi.Err() != nil {\\n1083: \\t\\t\\treturn\\n1084: \\t\\t}\\n1085: \\n1086: \\titerate:\\n1087: \\t\\tfor {\\n1088: \\t\\t\\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\\n1089: ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\\n1099: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\\n1100: \\t\\t\\t\\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\\n1101: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\\n1102: \\t\\t\\t\\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\\n1103: \\t\\t\\t\\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\\n1104: \\t\\t\\t\\t//\\n1105: \\t\\t\\t\\t// If we receive ENOSPC failures, we will try to \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1118: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1119: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1120: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue retry\\n1121: \\t\\t\\t\\t} With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\n704: // retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n705: //\n706: // To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\n707: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\n708: \tif cb == nil {\n709: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n710: \t}\n711: \n712: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n713: \t\treturn err\n714: \t}\n715: \n716: \tm.lock.RLock()\n717: \tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n718: \n719: \t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n720: \tmk := m.key.New()\n721: \tmv := m.value.New()\n722: \n723: \ti := m.m.Iterate()\n724: \tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n725: \t\tcb(mk, mv)\n726: \n727: \t\tmk = m.key.New()\n728: \t\tmv = m.value.New()\n729: \t}\n730: \n731: \treturn i.Err()\n732: }\n733: \n734: // DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\n735: // the slice of all values from all CPUs.\n736: type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n737: \n738: // DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\n739: // DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\n740: // from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\n741: // to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n742: func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\n743: \tif cb == nil {\n744: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n745: \t}\n746: \n747: \tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\n748: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\", m.name)\n749: \t}\n750: \n751: \tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\n752: \tif !ok {\n753: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\", m.name)\n754: \t}\n755: \n756: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n757: \t\treturn err\n758: \t}\n759: \n760: \tm.lock.RLock()\n761: \tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n762: \n763: \t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n764: \tmk := m.key.New()\n765: \tmv := v.NewSlice()\n766: \n767: \ti := m.m.Iterate()\n768: \tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n769: \t\tcb(mk, mv)\n770: \n771: \t\tmk = m.key.New()\n772: \t\tmv = v.NewSlice()\n773: \t}\n774: \n775: \treturn i.Err()\n776: }\n777: \n778: // DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\n779: // if the given map does not exist.\n780: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\n781: \tfound, err := m.exist()\n782: \tif err != nil {\n783: \t\treturn err\n784: \t}\n785: \n786: \tif found {\n787: \t\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \treturn nil\n791: }\n792: \n793: // DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\n794: // additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\n795: // element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\n796: // can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\n797: // In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\n798: // the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\n799: //\n800: // The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\n801: // object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\n802: // not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\n803: func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n804: \tif cb == nil {\n805: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n806: \t}\n807: \n808: \tif stats == nil {\n809: \t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n810: \t}\n811: \n812: \tvar (\n813: \t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n814: \t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n815: \t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n816: \t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n817: \n818: \t\tprevKeyValid = false\n819: \t)\n820: \n821: \tstats.start()\n822: \tdefer stats.finish()\n823: \n824: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n825: \t\treturn err\n826: \t}\n827: \n828: \t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\n829: \t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\n830: \t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\n831: \tm.lock.Lock()\n832: \tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n833: \tif m.m == nil {\n834: \t\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\n835: \t\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\n836: \t\treturn errors.New(\"map is closed\")\n837: \t}\n838: \n839: \t// Get the first map key.\n840: \tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\n841: \t\tstats.Lookup = 1\n842: \t\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n843: \t\t\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\n844: \t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n845: \t\t\treturn nil\n846: \t\t}\n847: \t}\n848: \n849: \t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\n850: \t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\n851: \t// updated while being iterated)\n852: \tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\n853: \n854: \t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\n855: \t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\n856: \t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\n857: \tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\n858: \t\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\n859: \t\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\n860: \t\t//\n861: \t\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\n862: \t\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\n863: \t\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\n864: \t\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\n865: \t\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\n866: \n867: \t\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\n868: \t\t\tstats.LookupFailed++\n869: \t\t\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\n870: \t\t\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\n871: \t\t\tif prevKeyValid {\n872: \t\t\t\tcurrentKey = prevKey\n873: \t\t\t\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\n874: \t\t\t\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\n875: \t\t\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n876: \t\t\t\tstats.KeyFallback++\n877: \t\t\t} else {\n878: \t\t\t\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\n879: \t\t\t\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\n880: \t\t\t\t// one, or the first element in the map.\n881: \t\t\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n882: \t\t\t\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\n883: \t\t\t\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\n884: \t\t\t\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\n885: \t\t\t\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\n886: \t\t\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n887: \t\t\t\tstats.Interrupted++\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t\tcontinue\n890: \t\t}\n891: \n892: \t\tcb(currentKey, value)\n893: \n894: \t\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\n895: \t\t\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n896: \t\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n897: \t\t\t\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\n898: \t\t\t}\n899: \t\t\treturn nextKeyErr\n900: \t\t}\n901: \n902: \t\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\n903: \t\tprevKey = currentKey\n904: \t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n905: \t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n906: \t\tprevKeyValid = true\n907: \t}\n908: \n909: \treturn ErrMaxLookup\n910: }\n911: \n912: // BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\n913: // of bpf maps.\n914: type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n915: \tm    *Map\n916: \terr  error\n917: \tkeys []KT\n918: \tvals []VT\n919: \n920: \tchunkSize      int\n921: \tmaxDumpRetries uint32\n922: \n923: \t// Iteration stats\n924: \tbatchSize int\n925: \n926: \topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\n927: }\n928: \n929: // NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\n930: // This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\n931: // when end of map is reached.\n932: // Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\n933: // the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\n934: // The pointer type of KT & VT must implement Map{Key,Value}, respectively.\n935: //\n936: // Subsequent iterations via IterateAll reset all internal state and begin\n937: // iteration over.\n938: //\n939: // Example usage:\n940: //\n941: //\tm := NewMap(\"cilium_test\",\n942: //\t\tebpf.Hash,\n943: //\t\t&TestKey{}, \t// *TestKey implements MapKey.\n944: //\t\t&TestValue{}, \t// *TestValue implements MapValue.\n945: //\t\tmapSize,\n946: //\t\tBPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n947: //\t)\n948: //\n949: //\titer := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\n950: //\tfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n951: //\t\t// ...\n952: //\t}\n953: func NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n954: \treturn &BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]{\n955: \t\tm: m,\n956: \t}\n957: }\n958: \n959: // KeyPointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n960: // of a type T is a MapKey.\n961: type KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n962: \tMapKey\n963: \t*T\n964: }\n965: \n966: // ValuePointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n967: // of a type T is a MapValue.\n968: type ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n969: \tMapValue\n970: \t*T\n971: }\n972: \n973: // Err returns errors encountered during the previous iteration when\n974: // IterateAll(...) is called.\n975: //\n976: // If the iterator is reused, the error will be reset,\n977: func (kvs BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error {\n978: \treturn kvs.err\n979: }\n980: \n981: func (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\n982: \tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\n983: \t\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\n984: \t}\n985: \treturn defaultBatchedRetries\n986: }\n987: \n988: const defaultBatchedRetries = 3\n989: \n990: type BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] func(*BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n991: \n992: // WithEBPFBatchOpts returns a batch iterator option that allows for overriding\n993: // BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH options.\n994: func WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n995: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n996: \t\tin.opts = opts\n997: \t\treturn in\n998: \t}\n999: }\n1000: \n1001: // WithMaxRetries returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the default\n1002: // max batch retries.\n1003: //\n1004: // Unless the starting chunk size is set to be the map size, it is possible for iteration\n1005: // to fail with ENOSPC if the passed allocated chunk array size is not big enough to accommodate\n1006: // a the bpf maps underlying hashmaps bucket size.\n1007: //\n1008: // If this happens, BatchIterator will automatically attempt to double the batch size and\n1009: // retry the iteration from the same place - up to a number of retries.\n1010: func WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1011: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1012: \t\tin.maxDumpRetries = retries\n1013: \t\treturn in\n1014: \t}\n1015: }\n1016: \n1017: // WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\n1018: // chosen starting chunk size.\n1019: func WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1020: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1021: \t\tin.chunkSize = size\n1022: \t\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\n1023: \t\t\tin.chunkSize = 8\n1024: \t\t}\n1025: \t\treturn in\n1026: \t}\n1027: }\n1028: \n1029: // CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\n1030: // iterator.\n1031: func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\n1032: \tc := 0\n1033: \tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n1034: \t\tc++\n1035: \t}\n1036: \treturn c, iter.Err()\n1037: }\n1038: \n1039: func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\n1040: \tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\n1041: \tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\n1042: \treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\n1043: }\n1044: \n1045: // IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\n1046: // using the batched API.\n1047: // In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\n1048: // this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\n1049: // of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\n1050: // If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\n1051: // will be returned via Err().\n1052: //\n1053: // All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\n1054: //\n1055: // If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will return the error that caused the failure.\n1056: func (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP] {\n1057: \tswitch bi.m.Type() {\n1058: \tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\n1059: \t\tbreak\n1060: \tdefault:\n1061: \t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\", bi.m.Type())\n1062: \t\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\n1063: \t}\n1064: \n1065: \tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\n1066: \n1067: \tfor _, opt := range opts {\n1068: \t\tif opt != nil {\n1069: \t\t\tbi = opt(bi)\n1070: \t\t}\n1071: \t}\n1072: \n1073: \t// reset values\n1074: \tbi.err = nil\n1075: \tbi.batchSize = 0\n1076: \tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n1077: \tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n1078: \n1079: \tprocessed := 0\n1080: \tvar cursor ebpf.MapBatchCursor\n1081: \treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {\n1082: \t\tif bi.Err() != nil {\n1083: \t\t\treturn\n1084: \t\t}\n1085: \n1086: \titerate:\n1087: \t\tfor {\n1088: \t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n1089: \t\t\t\tbi.err = ctx.Err()\n1090: \t\t\t\treturn\n1091: \t\t\t}\n1092: \t\tretry:\n1093: \t\t\tfor retry := range bi.maxBatchedRetries() {\n1094: \t\t\t\t// Attempt to read batch into buffer.\n1095: \t\t\t\tc, batchErr := bi.m.BatchLookup(&cursor, bi.keys, bi.vals, nil)\n1096: \t\t\t\tbi.batchSize = c\n1097: \n1098: \t\t\t\tdone := errors.Is(batchErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\n1099: \t\t\t\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\n1100: \t\t\t\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\n1101: \t\t\t\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\n1102: \t\t\t\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\n1103: \t\t\t\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\n1104: \t\t\t\t//\n1105: \t\t\t\t// If we receive ENOSPC failures, we will try to recover by growing the batch buffer\n1106: \t\t\t\t// size (up to some max number of retries - default: 3) and retrying the iteration.\n1107: \t\t\t\t//\n1108: \t\t\t\t// [1] https://elixir.bootlin.com/linux/v6.12.6/source/kernel/bpf/hashtab.c#L1807-L1809\n1109: \t\t\t\t//\n1110: \t\t\t\t// Note: If this failure happens during the bpf syscall, it is expected that the underlying\n1111: \t\t\t\t// cursor will not have been swapped - meaning that we can retry the iteration at the same cursor.\n1112: \t\t\t\tif errors.Is(batchErr, unix.ENOSPC) {\n1113: \t\t\t\t\tif retry == bi.maxBatchedRetries()-1 {\n1114: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.err = batchErr\n1115: \t\t\t\t\t} else {\n1116: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.chunkSize *= 2\n1117: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n1118: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n1119: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1120: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue retry\n1121: \t\t\t\t} else if !done && batchErr != nil {\n1122: \t\t\t\t\t// If we're not done, and we didn't hit a ENOSPC then stop iteration and record\n1123: \t\t\t\t\t// the error.\n1124: \t\t\t\t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"failed to iterate map: %w\", batchErr)\n1125: \t\t\t\t\treturn\n1126: \t\t\t\t}\n1127: \n1128: \t\t\t\t// Yield all received pairs.\n1129: \t\t\t\tfor i := range bi.batchSize {\n1130: \t\t\t\t\tprocessed++\n1131: \t\t\t\t\tif !yield(&bi.keys[i], &bi.vals[i]) {\n1132: \t\t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n1133: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1134: \t\t\t\t}\n1135: \n1136: \t\t\t\tif done {\n1137: \t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n1138: \t\t\t\t}\n1139: \t\t\t\tbreak retry // finish retry loop for this batch.\n1140: \t\t\t}\n1141: \t\t}\n1142: \t}\n1143: }\n1144: \n1145: // Dump returns the map (type map[string][]string) which contains all\n1146: // data stored in BPF map.\n1147: func (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error {\n1148: \tcallback := func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n1149: \t\t// No need to deep copy since we are creating \t// decoder.\n155: \tkeys := make(nopDecoder, chunkSize)\n156: \tvals := make(nopDecoder, chunkSize)\n157: \tmaxRetries := defaultBatchedRetries\n158: \n159: \tvar cursor ebpf.MapBatchCursor\n160: For example, code can be moved from one tail\n94: // call to another, making some instructions execute twice or not at all\n95: // depending on the order the tail calls were inserted.\n96: func mapsToReplace(toReplace []string, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, coll *ebpf.Collection, opts ebpf.CollectionOptions) ([]toPin, error) {\n97: \tif opts.Maps.PinPath == \"\" && len(toReplace) > 0 {\n98: \t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"empty Maps.PinPath in CollectionOptions\")\n99: \t}\n100: \n101: \t// We need both Map and MapSpec as the pin path is derived from MapSpec.Name,\n102: \t// and can be modified before creating the Collection. This is to be called after the Collection's programs have\n128: // been attached to the required hooks. Any existing pins are overwritten.\n129: func commitMapPins(logger *slog.Logger, pins []toPin) error {\n130: \tfor _, pin := range pins {\n131: \t\tif err := os.Remove(pin.path); err != nil && !errors.Is(err, os.ErrNotExist) {\n132: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"removing map pin at %s: %w\", pin.path, err)\n133: \t\t}\n134: \t\tif err := pin.m.Pin(pin.path); err != nil {\n135: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"pinning map to %s: %w\", pin.path, err)\n136: \t\t}\n137: \n138: \t\tlogger.Debug(\"Replaced map pin\", logfields.Pin, pin.path)\n139: \t}\n140: \n141: \treturn nil\n142: }\n143: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/cilium--ad6b298d@7e98f10a7fa8937a3e19078d2426107b6dd2b121/-/blob/pkg/bpf/pinning.go"}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01WA4bae6j8vu1oNjNYS6iDm","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01HwHk37hrgQ8tbxnknSTN9M","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Cilium eBPF map package provides a comprehensive Go wrapper API for user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps. It abstracts the complexity of eBPF syscalls while providing high-level operations for managing maps, inserting data, iterating entries, and maintaining map state.\n\n## Core Concepts\n\n### Map Lifecycle\n\nMaps follow a clear lifecycle:\n1. **Creation**: Create a Map instance using `NewMap()` or `NewMapWithInnerSpec()`\n2. **Opening/Creating**: Call `OpenOrCreate()` to open an existing map or create a new one\n3. **Operations**: Perform CRUD operations while the map is open\n4. **Closing**: Call `Close()` to close the map (optional if you want to keep it open)\n\n### MapKey and MapValue Interfaces\n\nAll key and value types used with maps must implement these interfaces:\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New must return a pointer to a new instance of the key type\n    New() MapKey\n}\n\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New must return a pointer to a new instance of the value type\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\nFor per-CPU maps, values must additionally implement:\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n    // NewSlice returns a pointer to a slice of values, one per CPU\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n**Example Implementation**:\n\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        [16]byte // IPv6 or IPv4 in lowest 4 bytes\n    Family    uint8\n    Key       uint8\n    ClusterID uint16\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) String() string {\n    // Return human-readable representation\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"endpoint:%s\", k.IP)\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n```\n\n## Core Map Type and Creation\n\n### Creating a Map Instance\n\n```go\n// NewMap creates a new Map instance with the given parameters\n// Does not automatically open or create the map in the kernel\nfunc NewMap(\n    name string,                    // Map name (used for pinning)\n    mapType ebpf.MapType,          // e.g., ebpf.Hash, ebpf.Array\n    mapKey MapKey,                  // Sample key (used for size calculation)\n    mapValue MapValue,              // Sample value (used for size calculation)\n    maxEntries int,                 // Maximum entries in the map\n    flags uint32,                   // eBPF map flags (e.g., BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC)\n) *Map\n```\n\nMaps are not created in the kernel until you call `OpenOrCreate()` or `Create()`.\n\n### Creating Maps with Inner Maps\n\n```go\n// NewMapWithInnerSpec creates a Map with an inner map specification\n// Useful for creating map-of-maps structures\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(\n    name string,\n    mapType ebpf.MapType,\n    mapKey MapKey,\n    mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int,\n    flags uint32,\n    innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec,  // Specification for the inner map\n) *Map\n```\n\n### Opening and Creating Maps\n\n```go\n// OpenOrCreate opens an existing map or creates a new one\n// If a map already exists but is incompatible (different type, size, etc.),\n// it will be deleted and recreated, losing all data\n// Maps are automatically pinned to the BPF filesystem\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n\n// CreateUnpinned creates the map without pinning it to the filesystem\n// The map will not persist after the map object is closed\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n\n// Create opens or creates the map, then immediately closes it\n// Useful for initialization without keeping the map open\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n\n// Open opens an existing pinned map from the filesystem\n// Returns an error if the map does not exist\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n\n// IsOpen returns whether the map is currently open\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n\n// Recreate removes the pinned map, recreates it, and re-pins it\n// Useful for resetting map state\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\n### Closing Maps\n\n```go\n// Close closes the map file descriptor\n// Does not unpin the map from the filesystem\n// After closing, the map can be reopened with Open() or OpenOrCreate()\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup Operations\n\n```go\n// Lookup retrieves a value by key\n// Opens the map if not already open\n// Returns the value or an error if not found\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Automatically opens the map if needed\n- Returns nil value and error if key not found\n- Safe to call concurrently (uses read lock)\n\n### Insert/Update Operations\n\n```go\n// Update inserts or updates a key-value pair\n// Creates or opens the map automatically\n// Updates all events and cache state\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Automatically opens/creates the map if needed\n- Overwrites existing values\n- If caching is enabled, updates cache and marks entry as synced\n- If an error occurs, marks entry for deferred resolution\n- Emits update events if events buffer is enabled\n\n### Delete Operations\n\n```go\n// Delete removes a key from the map\n// Returns an error if the key does not exist\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n\n// SilentDelete removes a key from the map\n// Returns (false, nil) if the key does not exist (no error)\n// Useful for cleanup operations where missing keys are acceptable\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n\n// DeleteLocked removes a key from the map when m.lock is already held\n// Must be called from within a DumpCallback to avoid deadlocks\n// Used when deleting during iteration\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n\n// DeleteAll removes all entries from the map\n// Iterates and deletes individual entries\n// Entries added during deletion may survive the operation\n// Updates cache if enabled\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n\n// ClearAll empties the map by setting all values to zero\n// Only works if events buffer and value cache are disabled\n// Faster than DeleteAll for certain use cases\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\n**Deletion Semantics**:\n- All delete operations update the event buffer if enabled\n- Cache entries are marked for deletion and removed on successful delete\n- If deletion fails, the cache entry is updated with the error for later retry\n- `DeleteLocked` must be used when deleting within a `DumpCallback` to avoid deadlock\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### Simple Iteration with Callback\n\n```go\n// DumpCallback is the callback function type for map iteration\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n\n// DumpWithCallback iterates all entries and calls the callback for each\n// Opens the map if not already open\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n\n// DumpWithCallbackIfExists is like DumpWithCallback but returns early if map doesn't exist\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\n**Per-CPU Maps**:\n\n```go\n// DumpPerCPUCallback receives all values from all CPUs for a single key\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\n// DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates per-CPU maps, providing all CPU values for each key\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\n### Reliable Iteration with Statistics\n\nFor cases where the map is being modified concurrently, use reliable dumping:\n\n```go\n// DumpReliablyWithCallback iterates the map with backtracking support\n// Handles concurrent modifications by falling back to previously seen keys\n// Limits iterations to 4x the map size to prevent infinite loops\n// Returns ErrMaxLookup if iteration limit exceeded\n//\n// The callback must not invoke map operations that acquire m.lock\n// to avoid deadlock\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(\n    cb DumpCallback,\n    stats *DumpStats,\n) error\n\n// DumpStats tracks iteration statistics\ntype DumpStats struct {\n    Started        time.Time  // When iteration began\n    Finished       time.Time  // When iteration ended\n    Lookup         uint32     // Number of key lookups performed\n    LookupFailed   uint32     // Failed lookups during iteration\n    KeyFallback    uint32     // Times we fell back to previous key\n    Interrupted    uint32     // Times iteration was interrupted\n    MaxEntries     uint32     // Maximum entries in map\n    Completed      bool       // Whether iteration completed successfully\n}\n\n// NewDumpStats creates a DumpStats for tracking iteration\nfunc NewDumpStats(m *Map) *DumpStats\n\n// Duration returns the total iteration time\nfunc (d *DumpStats) Duration() time.Duration\n```\n\n### Hash Map Dump\n\n```go\n// Dump returns a map of all key-value pairs as strings\n// Useful for debugging and API responses\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n\n// DumpIfExists calls Dump only if the map exists on the filesystem\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\n## Batch Iteration\n\nFor better performance when iterating large maps, use the batch iterator:\n\n```go\n// BatchIterator provides typed batch iteration over maps\n// Automatically handles buffer sizing when ENOSPC occurs\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n    // Contains internal state, do not modify directly\n}\n\n// NewBatchIterator creates a batch iterator for the map\n// The pointer types KP and VP must implement MapKey and MapValue\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    m *Map,\n) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n\n// IterateAll returns an iterator sequence over all map entries\n// Automatically retries with larger buffers if ENOSPC occurs\n// Respects context cancellation\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(\n    ctx context.Context,\n    opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP],\n) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n\n// Err returns any error encountered during iteration\n// Reset to nil when IterateAll is called again\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error\n```\n\n**Batch Iterator Options**:\n\n```go\n// WithStartingChunkSize sets the initial batch size\n// Default is calculated from sqrt(max_entries * 2)\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    size int,\n) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n\n// WithMaxRetries sets maximum retry attempts for ENOSPC errors\n// Default is 3\nfunc WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    retries uint32,\n) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n\n// WithEBPFBatchOpts passes custom batch options to the kernel\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    opts *ebpf.BatchOptions,\n) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n\n// CountAll is a helper that returns the total number of entries\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    ctx context.Context,\n    iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP],\n) (int, error)\n```\n\n**Batch Iterator Example**:\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](myMap)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    // Process k and v\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    // Handle iteration error\n}\n```\n\n**ENOSPC Handling**: The batch iterator automatically handles `ENOSPC` errors by doubling the buffer size and retrying. If retries are exhausted, the error is returned via `Err()`.\n\n### Low-Level Batch Operations\n\n```go\n// BatchLookup performs a batch lookup operation\n// Returns the count of items retrieved\nfunc (m *Map) BatchLookup(\n    cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor,\n    keysOut, valuesOut any,\n    opts *ebpf.BatchOptions,\n) (int, error)\n\n// BatchCount counts entries using batch lookup (Hash/LRUHash/LPMTrie only)\n// Automatically handles buffer sizing\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\nMaps can be pinned to the BPF filesystem, allowing persistence across application restarts:\n\n```go\n// Pin status depends on how the map was created:\n// - OpenOrCreate() and Create(): Maps are automatically pinned\n// - CreateUnpinned(): Maps are not pinned and will be deleted on close\n\n// Path returns the filesystem path where the map is pinned\n// Automatically sets the path based on the map name if not already set\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n\n// Unpin removes the pinned map from the filesystem\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n\n// UnpinIfExists unpins the map only if it exists on the filesystem\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\n### BPF Filesystem Paths\n\n```go\n// BPFFSRoot returns the root path of the mounted BPF filesystem\n// Typically /sys/fs/bpf on Linux systems\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n\n// CiliumPath returns the Cilium-specific BPF filesystem path\n// Typically <bpffs>/cilium\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n\n// MapPath returns the absolute path for a map with the given name\n// Used to construct pinning paths\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n\n// LocalMapName returns a name for a map local to a specific ID\n// Pattern: basename + 5-digit zero-padded ID\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\n\n// LocalMapPath returns the path for a local map\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\n## Event System\n\nMaps can emit events for all operations, enabling real-time monitoring:\n\n```go\n// Action describes the type of event\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate   Action = iota  // Key-value pair was added/updated\n    MapDelete                   // Key was deleted\n    MapDeleteAll                // All entries were deleted (aggregated event)\n)\n\n// Event contains information about a map operation\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time  // When the operation occurred\n    // Internal fields (access via GetAction, GetKey, GetValue, etc.)\n}\n\n// GetAction returns the action type as a string\nfunc (e *Event) GetAction() string\n\n// GetKey returns the key as a string\nfunc (e Event) GetKey() string\n\n// GetValue returns the value as a string (or \"<nil>\" for deletes)\nfunc (e Event) GetValue() string\n\n// GetLastError returns the error if the operation failed\nfunc (e Event) GetLastError() error\n\n// GetDesiredAction returns the current sync state of the entry\nfunc (e Event) GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction\n```\n\n### Event Subscription\n\n```go\n// EventCallbackFunc processes events from the event buffer\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n\n// DumpAndSubscribe dumps existing events and optionally subscribes to new ones\n// If follow is true, the callback will continue receiving new events\n// The callback must handle events until context is cancelled\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(\n    ctx context.Context,\n    callback EventCallbackFunc,\n    follow bool,\n) error\n\n// IsEventsEnabled returns whether events are enabled for this map\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\n### Enabling Events\n\nEvents are enabled via configuration:\n\n```go\n// WithEvents enables the event buffer with given configuration\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nThe event buffer stores a bounded ring buffer of recent events. Old events are automatically garbage-collected based on TTL.\n\n## Caching and Synchronization\n\nMaps can maintain a local cache of entries for faster lookups and error recovery:\n\n```go\n// WithCache enables value caching and error synchronization\n// Cached entries track the DesiredAction (OK, Insert, Delete)\n// and LastError from the last operation\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map\n```\n\n**Cache Behavior**:\n- When `Update()` fails, the cache marks the entry for Insert and schedules error resolution\n- When `Delete()` fails, the cache marks the entry for Delete and schedules error resolution\n- A periodic error resolver attempts to resync failed entries\n- Cache is useful for detecting sync issues and enabling recovery\n\n### Pressure Metrics\n\nTrack map utilization via metrics:\n\n```go\n// WithPressureMetric enables pressure tracking with threshold 0\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map\n\n// WithPressureMetricThreshold enables pressure tracking with a custom threshold\n// Pressure is calculated as (cache_size / max_entries)\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(\n    registry *metrics.Registry,\n    threshold float64,\n) *Map\n\n// UpdatePressureMetricWithSize manually updates the pressure metric\nfunc (m *Map) UpdatePressureMetricWithSize(size int32)\n```\n\n## Builder Methods\n\nMaps support method chaining for configuration:\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &MyKey{}, &MyValue{}, 1000, 0).\n    WithCache().\n    WithEvents(eventConfig).\n    WithPressureMetric(registry).\n    WithGroupName(\"my_group\")\n\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    // Handle error\n}\n```\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nFor complex eBPF programs with multiple maps:\n\n```go\n// CollectionOptions configures the loading process\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants for datapath runtime configuration\n    Constants any\n\n    // Maps to rename during loading\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // Map replacements (pass existing Maps)\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Objects to keep during reachability pruning\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // Path to write configuration dump\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n\n// LoadCollection loads an eBPF collection spec into the kernel\n// Returns a function that must be called after attaching all programs\n// This function commits map pins to the filesystem\nfunc LoadCollection(\n    logger *slog.Logger,\n    spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions,\n) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n\n// LoadAndAssign loads a collection and assigns objects to struct fields\n// Analyzes the target struct to determine which maps to keep\nfunc LoadAndAssign(\n    logger *slog.Logger,\n    to any,\n    spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions,\n) (func() error, error)\n```\n\n**Collection Loading Workflow**:\n\n1. Create a `CollectionSpec` (usually from an ELF file)\n2. Call `LoadCollection()` or `LoadAndAssign()` with options\n3. Attach programs to their kernel hooks\n4. Call the returned `commit()` function to finalize map pinning\n\nThis two-phase approach ensures tail call maps are populated correctly after program attachment.\n\n## Metadata and Utilities\n\n```go\n// Name returns the basename of the map\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string\n\n// Type returns the map type (Hash, Array, etc.)\nfunc (m *Map) Type() ebpf.MapType\n\n// KeySize returns the size of keys in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) KeySize() uint32\n\n// ValueSize returns the size of values in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) ValueSize() uint32\n\n// MaxEntries returns the maximum number of entries\nfunc (m *Map) MaxEntries() uint32\n\n// Flags returns the eBPF flags set on the map\nfunc (m *Map) Flags() uint32\n\n// FD returns the file descriptor of the opened map\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int\n\n// NonPrefixedName returns the name without the metrics namespace prefix\nfunc (m *Map) NonPrefixedName() string\n\n// GetModel returns a JSON-serializable representation of the map\n// Includes cache contents if caching is enabled\nfunc (m *Map) GetModel() *models.BPFMap\n```\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Errors\n\n```go\n// ErrMaxLookup is returned when DumpReliablyWithCallback exceeds\n// the iteration limit (4x map size)\nErrMaxLookup = errors.New(\"maximum number of lookups reached\")\n\n// ErrMapNotOpened is returned by map operations if the map is not open\nErrMapNotOpened = errors.New(\"BPF map has not been opened\")\n\n// ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist is returned when a key is not found in Lookup\n// Use errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) to check\n\n// unix.ENOSPC is returned when batch buffers are too small\n// BatchIterator handles this automatically\n```\n\n### Error Resolution\n\nWhen operations fail and caching is enabled, errors are tracked and resolved:\n\n```go\n// DesiredAction indicates the sync state of a cached entry\ntype DesiredAction uint8\n\nconst (\n    OK     DesiredAction = iota  // Entry is synced\n    Insert                       // Entry needs to be inserted/updated\n    Delete                       // Entry needs to be deleted\n)\n```\n\nEntries with outstanding errors are automatically resolved by a periodic controller.\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Map Operations\n\n```go\n// Create and open a map\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &MyKey{},\n    &MyValue{},\n    1000,\n    0,\n)\ndefer m.Close()\n\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Insert\nif err := m.Update(&MyKey{ID: 1}, &MyValue{Data: 42}); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Lookup\nval, err := m.Lookup(&MyKey{ID: 1})\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Delete\nif err := m.Delete(&MyKey{ID: 1}); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### Iterating with Batch API\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](m)\n\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", k, v)\n}\n\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### Iteration with Callbacks and Deletion\n\n```go\n// Delete entries matching a condition\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(\n    func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n        k := key.(*MyKey)\n        if k.ShouldDelete() {\n            // Must use DeleteLocked since we're in a callback\n            if err := m.DeleteLocked(k); err != nil {\n                // Log error\n            }\n        }\n    },\n    NewDumpStats(m),\n)\n```\n\n### Event Monitoring\n\n```go\nm.WithEvents(eventConfig)\n\ngo func() {\n    m.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(event Event) {\n        fmt.Printf(\"[%s] %s -> %s\\n\",\n            event.GetAction(),\n            event.GetKey(),\n            event.GetValue(),\n        )\n    }, true)  // true = follow new events\n}()\n```\n\n### Per-CPU Map Operations\n\n```go\ntype MyPerCPUValue struct {\n    Counter uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyPerCPUValue) NewSlice() any {\n    return &[]MyPerCPUValue{}\n}\n\nm := NewMap(\"per_cpu_map\",\n    ebpf.PerCPUHash,\n    &MyKey{},\n    &MyPerCPUValue{},\n    1000,\n    0,\n)\n\nm.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    vals := values.(*[]MyPerCPUValue)\n    total := uint64(0)\n    for _, v := range *vals {\n        total += v.Counter\n    }\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key %s total: %d\\n\", key, total)\n})\n```\n\n### Loading Complex Programs\n\n```go\nopts := &CollectionOptions{\n    MapRenames: []map[string]string{\n        {\"old_name\": \"new_name\"},\n    },\n    Constants: &myConfig,\n}\n\ncoll, commit, err := LoadCollection(logger, spec, opts)\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Attach programs from coll to kernel hooks\n// ...\n\n// Call commit after all programs are attached\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n## Thread Safety\n\nMaps are designed for concurrent access:\n\n- `Lookup()` acquires a read lock and is safe for concurrent calls\n- `Update()` and `Delete()` acquire a write lock\n- `DumpWithCallback()` acquires a read lock\n- `DumpReliablyWithCallback()` acquires a write lock (to allow deletions in callback)\n- `DumpAndSubscribe()` acquires a read lock for the dump phase\n- Callbacks should avoid acquiring additional locks to prevent deadlocks\n\n## Memory Management\n\n- Maps automatically manage kernel map memory\n- Per-CPU maps allocate one value per CPU core\n- Event buffers use a ring buffer that automatically evicts old events\n- Cache size is bounded by map size\n- Pinned maps persist in the BPF filesystem until explicitly unpinned\n\n## Supported Map Types\n\nThe API works with all standard eBPF map types:\n\n- **Hash**: Standard hash table map\n- **Array**: Indexed array (0 to max_entries-1)\n- **PerCPUHash**: Hash table with per-CPU values\n- **PerCPUArray**: Array with per-CPU values\n- **LRUHash**: Hash table with automatic LRU eviction\n- **LRUCPUHash**: Per-CPU hash with LRU eviction\n- **LPMTrie**: Longest prefix match trie for IP routing\n\nBatch iteration and batch operations only work with Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie maps.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2351,"cache_read_input_tokens":81952,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2351,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"fdc5ecb0-dd8d-4f0a-8441-9ae5c4ce4f5c","uuid":"3e9d8ecd-980e-4fba-a0b6-91c88e60081d"}
